# File: r_info.txt
# Reworked for GSNband 1.0

# This file is used to initialize the "lib/raw/r_info.raw" file, which is
# used to initialize the "monster race" information for the Angband game.

# Do not modify this file unless you know exactly what you are doing,
# unless you wish to risk possible system crashes and broken savefiles.

# Sources of monsters:

# The largest bulk (> 500 entries) comes from vanilla Angband. Practically
# every monster found there is retained in GSNband, with the exception of
# ICEish Nazguls

# Over 200 monsters came over from ZAngband. Those include both the original
# set designed by Topi Ylinen and later additions by RR

# Kamband has been the source of another ~100 monsters, particularly those
# that damage sanity and/or live in water, and the FHotA

# From OAngband I took Eol, Maeglin, Ar-Pharazon, two vortices, and others

# From SAngband I took the Lucksucker, Pink Elephant, and the Spectral Killers
# family

# From JAngband I took three high-level trolls and Muar, the original Moria
# Balrog (tm)

# From DrAngband I took several * monsters, the Storm Knight, Antimagic
# Hound, and others

# Paasi Huttunen created an alternative set of monsters designed for his
# own roleplaying world. I took over 30 monsters verbatim and several
# others as prototypes (Yeek Warriors etc.)

# Last but not least, I designed the XCOM-styled aliens and a few golems
# (the latter based on the M&M4 RPG world)

# Any monsters not coming from the above sources are probably minor
# contributions found on r.g.r.a., web pages, and such

# GSNband notes:

# Semantics of S_WRAITH: S_WRAITH now summons only normal wraiths, because
# all the 'special' wraiths introduced in vanilla for that purpose do
# not exist any more.

# Note that the third field in the W: line is unused. I'm going to insert
# monster size there (1 - tiny, 10 - gigantic, or similar scale)

# Summary of monster flags introduced as compared to ZAngband:
#   NOMISS - never misses in melee
#   DUNADAN - replaced AMBERITE, killing it invokes the dreaded TY_CURSE
#   HURT_ELEC, HURT_POIS, HURT_ACID - hurt by those types of attacks
#   AQUATIC - only created in water
#   CAN_FLY - can move over water/lava
#   CAN_SWIM - can move through water
#   UNFAIR - is considered unfair compared to its base depth
#   FRIENDLY - friendly monsters won't attack you in melee, nor with spells.
#              They will attack other monsters only if those are of opposite 
#	       alignment
#   PET - pet monsters follow you and can be given orders
#
#      Both friendly and pet monsters will 'rebel' if they're hurt by you.
#      Note that this doesn't mean actual HP loss, just influencing the
#      monster with something it doesn't like
#
#   RES_* and IM_* (where * = STAB, SLASH, BASH) - resistance (1/3 damage)
#   and almost-immunity (1/6 damage) to given type of weapons
#   RES_STON - resist stoning
#
#   And these are special flags for corpse-eating effects:
#   INFLATE - increases nutrition value five times
#   SLEEP - paralyze
#   FORGET - cause memory loss, as per spell
#   NEXUS - nexus effects, as per breath/spell
#   BLINK - blink, as per spell
#   MANA - restore mana
#   BLINDNESS, CONFUSION, VOMIT, BERSERK - obvious

# Note the special use of WILD_* flags: WILD_ONLY set alone means that the
# creature won't appear in the game except if set explicitly (in a quest,
# maybe). This is how the armies of good for the Lonely Mountain quest
# are handled. 

# Please follow the guidelines below when submitting new monsters:

# I only want monsters which are somehow connected to the Tolkienian
# universe. They may be animals mentioned in his works, for example. But
# any stuff which ICE manufactured for their MERP game is probably out
# of question. New uniques should be given extra caution - placing Gandalf
# and Morgoth in one row probably wasn't the brightest move ever, but
# this isn't a plot game, so such things are allowed

# I left Great Cthulhu and his minions alone because they're object of a
# quest which I didn't want to remove. Cthulhu is also a major god to
# the neutrals

# Monster aligments have been reworked. There are more good and fewer evil
# monsters. Creatures without GOOD or EVIL flags are considered 'unaligned',
# unless they're also animals, in which case those of neutral alignment can
# befriend them

# Neutral monsters (animals) should be contained in the following symbols:
# a, b, c, f, l, q, r, w, B, C, F, I, J, K, M, R, S, X, Z

# Monsters which are not letters should be unaligned, as should be some
# of E, e, n, v (the rest may be animals)

# g (golems) and x (aliens) are never aligned, perhaps also j and m, but
# evil molds are known to exist

# Undead monsters are almost exclusively evil. These include s, z, G, L, V, W.
# Other letter monsters can be evil & undead, but they should not be
# animals (the evil-ness takes precedence anyway)

# u and U should be evil, but non-alignment may be the case for some of the u
# and U's can be neutral if they're ELDRITCH_HORROR as well

# o, O, Q, T are evil without exception

# y (yeeks) are good denizens of the underground, as opposed to the evil
# k (kobolds) (as requested by AYAS - American Yeek Appreciation Society)

# p, P, h, H, d, D and t monsters are various humanoids and dragons, and
# can be either good, evil or unaligned. It's a pity we can't give them
# a random alignment. It is debatable whether Tolkienian dark elves
# should be evil (as opposed to the wicked AD&D Drows)

# A (angels) are exclusively good, with the possible exception of fallen
# angels & the like, but perhaps these shouldn't be A's in the first place.
# So are Y's.

# Monsters may be hurt by the four basic elements, and poison. Consider
# fire effective against creatures made of paper, ice and those that have
# a could aura (unless they also have fire attacks/spells). Cold works the 
# other way round. Electricity damages some water monsters (extra voltage in
# sea water), acid damages machines and plants (insects too?), and poison
# is a special case - I couldn't find many monsters susceptible to it, so
# let's pretend that the quylthulgs are badly affected by it, as they came
# from another world where other things are considered poison

# The rest of this intro comes from original Vanilla (slightly edited)
# by Ben Harrison

# ATTR_CLEAR monsters acquire their attr from the item/floor below them,
# and use "white" for the recall window.  See "cave.c" for info.

# ATTR_MULTI monsters have a "flickering" attr, and use "violet" for the
# recall window.  See "cave.c" for info.

# CHAR_CLEAR monsters use special symbols (.) as given below,
# and use those symbols for the recall window.  In theory, normally,
# these monsters cannot be targetted, and when examined look like normal
# floors, until the player "notices" them (perhaps check "awake").

# CHAR_MULTI monsters use special symbols (!, ?, =) as given below,
# and use those symbols for the recall window.  In theory, normally,
# these monsters cannot be targetted, and when examined look like normal
# objects, until the player "notices" them (perhaps check "awake").

# Note that there are (a few) normal monsters who are "violet" but not
# ATTR_MULTI, and a lot of monsters which are "white" but not ATTR_CLEAR.

# Note that currently both CHAR_CLEAR and CHAR_MULTI monsters are treated
# as normal monsters that are just a little hard to see.

# T[opi] Y[linen]: [...] The monster coloring has been
# changed 'back' to pre-2.7.* coloring in several cases. For example, I
# prefer "black" thief c[h]aracters. Also color can be (and should) be used to
# convey information, but more importantly it is a visual presentation
# of the creature and should be what the creature "looks" like.

# Mushrooms look just like food (and use the "," symbol for both the recall
# window and for normal display), Creeping coins look just like coins (and
# use the "$" symbol for both the recall window and for normal display), and
# Trappers/Lurkers can never be seen (and use the "." symbol for the recall
# window).  All other monsters use "alphabetic" symbols, and "alphabetic"
# symbols are used only for monsters.

# The "&" symbol is reserved for internal debugging use (null object). "N" 
# is unused, in case you had some very weird ideas. Numbers could be used
# for monsters, but I don't know of any RL game that does so.

# The "`" symbol is reserved as an "alternate" open door picture, since
# the "'" symbol looks like the "," symbol in some fonts (esp. IBM).

# Certain symbols ("X", "Y", "B", "l", "I", etc) are used by
# very few monsters, and could be reorganized somewhat.

# There are still too many "p" monsters, perhaps they should be broken up.

# As always, you can enforce any "visual picture" you want with a "pref file".

# Note that monster zero is used for the "player" picture.

# Version stamp (required)

V:2.8.1
